     <p>
      <b>
       ETA
      </b>
      (
      <small>
       Basque:
      </small>
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Basque" title="Help:IPA for Basque">
        [eta]
       </a>
      </span>
      ,
      <small>
       Spanish:
      </small>
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">
        [eta]
       </a>
      </span>
      ), an
      <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">
       acronym
      </a>
      for
      <b>
       Euskadi Ta Askatasuna
      </b>
      (
      <small>
       Basque pronunciation:
      </small>
      <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
       <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Basque" title="Help:IPA for Basque">
        [euskai ta askatasuna]
       </a>
      </span>
      ; "Basque Country and Freedom")
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      is an armed
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_nationalism" title="Basque nationalism">
       Basque nationalist
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Separatism" title="Separatism">
       separatist
      </a>
      organization in northern Spain and southwestern France. The group was founded in 1959 and has since evolved from a group promoting traditional
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Basque_culture" title="Basque culture">
       Basque culture
      </a>
      to a paramilitary group with the goal of gaining independence for the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(greater_region)" title="Basque Country (greater region)">
       Greater Basque Country
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goizargi.com_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-goizargi.com-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ETA is the main group within the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_National_Liberation_Movement" title="Basque National Liberation Movement">
       Basque National Liberation Movement
      </a>
      and is the most important participant in the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_conflict" title="Basque conflict">
       Basque conflict
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      Since 1968, ETA has been held responsible for killing 829 people, injuring thousands and undertaking dozens of kidnappings.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualities_eta_829_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-casualities_eta_829-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-casualties_total_basque_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-casualties_total_basque-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Victimas_MIR_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Victimas_MIR-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smithsonianmag.com_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-smithsonianmag.com-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The group is proscribed as a
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_designated_terrorist_groups" title="List of designated terrorist groups">
       terrorist group
      </a>
      by
      <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
       Spain
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
       France
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._State_Department_list_of_Foreign_Terrorist_Organizations" title="U.S. State Department list of Foreign Terrorist Organizations">
       United States
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eu-not-listed-anymore-2011_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-eu-not-listed-anymore-2011-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This convention is followed by a plurality of domestic and international media, which also refer to the group as "terrorists".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There are more than 400
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_National_Liberation_Movement_Prisoners" title="Basque National Liberation Movement Prisoners">
       imprisoned members
      </a>
      of the group in Spain, France, and other countries.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA declared ceasefires in 1989, 1996, 1998 and 2006, and subsequently broke them. On 5 September 2010, ETA declared a new ceasefire
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_5_sep_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-bbc_5_sep-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      that is still in force  on 20 October 2011 ETA announced a "definitive cessation of its armed activity".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC20111020_21-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC20111020-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On 24 November 2012, it was reported that the group was ready to negotiate a "definitive end" to its operations and disband completely.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_Eta_.27ready_to_disband.27_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC_Eta_.27ready_to_disband.27-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA's motto is
      <span lang="eu" xml:lang="eu">
       <i>
        Bietan jarrai
       </i>
      </span>
      ("Keep up on both"), referring to the two figures in its symbol, a snake (representing politics) wrapped around an axe (representing armed struggle).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
       <a href="#cite_note-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2">
        <a href="#Political_support">
         <span class="tocnumber">

         </span>
         <span class="toctext">
          Political support
         </span>
        </a>
        <ul>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">
       Structure
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Structure">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ArmaTiroPumEtaMilikiliklik26_8.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="543" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/ArmaTiroPumEtaMilikiliklik26_8.jpg/220px-ArmaTiroPumEtaMilikiliklik26_8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/ArmaTiroPumEtaMilikiliklik26_8.jpg/330px-ArmaTiroPumEtaMilikiliklik26_8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/ArmaTiroPumEtaMilikiliklik26_8.jpg/440px-ArmaTiroPumEtaMilikiliklik26_8.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ArmaTiroPumEtaMilikiliklik26_8.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        ETA members fire blanks during the
        <a href="/wiki/Euzko_Gudarostea" title="Euzko Gudarostea">
         Day of the Basque Soldier
        </a>
        of 2006
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      ETA has changed its internal structure on several occasions, commonly for security reasons. The group used to have a very hierarchical organization with a leading figure at the top, delegating into three substructures: the logistical, military and political sections. Reports from Spanish and French police point towards significant changes in ETA's structures in recent years. ETA has divided the three substructures into a total of eleven. The change was a response to recent captures, and possible infiltration, by the different law enforcement agencies. ETA's intention is to disperse its members and reduce the impact of detentions.
     </p>
     <p>
      The leading committee is formed by 7 to 11 individuals, and ETA's internal documentation refers to it as Zuba, an abbreviation of
      <i>
       Zuzendaritza Batzordea
      </i>
      (directorial committee). There is another committee named
      <i>
       Zuba-hitu
      </i>
      that functions as an advisory committee. The eleven different substructures are: logistics, politics, international relations with fraternal organisations, military operations, reserves, prisoner support, expropriation, information, recruitment, negotiation, and treasury.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
       <a href="#cite_note-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA's armed operations are organized in different
      <i>
       taldes
      </i>
      ("groups") or
      <i>
       commandos
      </i>
      , generally composed of three to five members, whose objective is to conduct attacks in a specific geographic zone.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      The
      <i>
       taldes
      </i>
      are coordinated by the
      <i>
       cpula militar
      </i>
      ("military
      <a href="/wiki/Cupola" title="Cupola">
       cupola
      </a>
      "). To supply the
      <i>
       taldes
      </i>
      , support groups maintain
      <a href="/wiki/Safe_house" title="Safe house">
       safe houses
      </a>
      and
      <i>
       zulos
      </i>
      (small rooms concealed in forests,
      <a href="/wiki/Garret" title="Garret">
       garrets
      </a>
      or underground, used to store arms, explosives or, sometimes, kidnapped people; the Basque word
      <i>
       zulo
      </i>
      literally means "hole"). The small cellars used to hide the people kidnapped are named by ETA and ETA's supporters "people's jails".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-La_Raz.C3.B3n_T.C3.A9cnico_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-La_Raz.C3.B3n_T.C3.A9cnico-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Currently the most common
      <i>
       commandos
      </i>
      are itinerant, not linked to any specific area, and thus are more difficult to capture.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
       <a href="#cite_note-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Among its members, ETA distinguishes between
      <i>
       legales/legalak
      </i>
      ("legal ones"), those members who do not have police records and live apparently normal lives;
      <i>
       liberados
      </i>
      ("liberated") members known to the police that are on ETA's payroll and working full-time for ETA; and
      <i>
       apoyos
      </i>
      ("support") who just give occasional help and logistics support to the group when required.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There are also the imprisoned members of the group, serving time scattered across Spain and France, that sometimes still have significant influence inside the organisation; and finally the
      <i>
       quemados
      </i>
      ("burnt out"), members freed after having been imprisoned or those that are suspected by the group of being under police vigilance. In the past there was also the figure of the deportees, expelled by the French government to remote countries where they live freely. France has since stopped the practice of deporting ETA members to other places than to Spain to be judged.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      ETA's internal bulletin is named
      <i>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zutabe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zutabe (page does not exist)">
        Zutabe
       </a>
      </i>
      ("Column"), replacing the earlier one (1962)
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Zutik_(publication)" title="Zutik (publication)">
        Zutik
       </a>
      </i>
      ("Standing").
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA also promotes the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Kale_borroka" title="Kale borroka">
        kale borroka
       </a>
      </i>
      ("street fight"), that is, violent acts against public transportation, political parties offices or cultural buildings, destruction of private property of politicians, police, military, journalist, council members, and anyone voicing criticism against ETA, bank offices, menaces, graffiti of political mottoes, and general rioting, usually using
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktails" title="Molotov cocktails">
       Molotov cocktails
      </a>
      . These groups are made up mostly of young people, who are directed through youth organisations (such as
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jarrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jarrai (page does not exist)">
       Jarrai
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Haika&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Haika (page does not exist)">
       Haika
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Segi_(organization)" title="Segi (organization)">
       Segi
      </a>
      ). Many of the present-day members of ETA started their collaboration with the group as participants in the
      <i>
       kale borroka
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_support">
       Political support
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Political support">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EuskadiTaAskatasunaMural.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2989" data-file-width="1792" height="367" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/EuskadiTaAskatasunaMural.JPG/220px-EuskadiTaAskatasunaMural.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/EuskadiTaAskatasunaMural.JPG/330px-EuskadiTaAskatasunaMural.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/18/EuskadiTaAskatasunaMural.JPG/440px-EuskadiTaAskatasunaMural.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EuskadiTaAskatasunaMural.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A pro-ETA mural in
        <a href="/wiki/Durango,_Biscay" title="Durango, Biscay">
         Durango, Biscay
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The political party
      <a href="/wiki/Batasuna" title="Batasuna">
       Batasuna
      </a>
      pursues the same political goals as ETA and does not condemn ETA's use of violence. Formerly known as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euskal_Herritarrok" title="Euskal Herritarrok">
       Euskal Herritarrok
      </a>
      and "
      <a href="/wiki/Herri_Batasuna" title="Herri Batasuna">
       Herri Batasuna
      </a>
      ", it is presently banned by the Spanish Supreme Court as an anti-democratic organisation following the Political Parties Law (
      <i>
       Ley de Partidos Polticos
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
       <a href="#cite_note-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ), It generally received 8% to 15% of the vote in the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">
       Basque Autonomous Community
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Batasuna's political status is controversial. It was considered to be the political wing of ETA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
       <a href="#cite_note-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
       <a href="#cite_note-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Moreover, after the investigations on the nature of the relationship between Batasuna and ETA by Judge
      <a href="/wiki/Baltasar_Garz%C3%B3n" title="Baltasar Garzn">
       Baltasar Garzn
      </a>
      , who suspended the activities of the political organisation and ordered police to shut down its headquarters, the
      <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Spain" title="Supreme Court of Spain">
       Supreme Court of Spain
      </a>
      finally declared Batasuna illegal on 18 March 2003. The court considered proven that Batasuna had links with ETA and that it constituted in fact part of ETA's structure. In 2003, the Constitutional Tribunal upheld the legality of the law.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      However, the party itself denies being the political wing of ETA,
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2009)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      despite the fact that double membership  simultaneous or alternative  between Batasuna and ETA is often recorded, such as with the cases of prominent Batasuna leaders like Josu Ternera,
      <a href="/wiki/Arnaldo_Otegi" title="Arnaldo Otegi">
       Arnaldo Otegi
      </a>
      , Jon Salaberria and others.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
       <a href="#cite_note-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jvjtfe_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-jvjtfe-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Spanish
      <a href="/wiki/Cortes_Generales" title="Cortes Generales">
       Cortes
      </a>
      (the Spanish Parliament) began the process of declaring the party illegal in August 2002 by issuing a bill entitled the
      <i>
       Ley de Partidos Polticos
      </i>
      which bars political parties that use violence to achieve political goals, promotes hatred against different groups or seek to destroy the democratic system. The bill passed the Cortes with a 304 to 16 vote.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
       <a href="#cite_note-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Many within the Basque nationalistic movement strongly disputed the Law, which they consider too draconian or even unconstitutional; alleging that any party could be made illegal almost by choice, simply for not clearly stating their opposition to an attack.
     </p>
     <p>
      Defenders of the new law argue that the
      <i>
       Ley de Partidos
      </i>
      does not necessarily require responses to individual acts of violence, but rather a declaration of principles explicitly rejecting violence as a means of achieving political goals. Defenders also argue that the ban of a political party is subject to judicial process, with all the guarantees of the State of Law. Batasuna has failed to produce such a statement. As of February 2008
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      other political parties linked to organizations such as
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Spain_(Reconstituted)" title="Communist Party of Spain (Reconstituted)">
        Partido Comunista de Espaa (reconstituido)
       </a>
      </i>
      have also been declared illegal, and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acci%C3%B3n_Nacionalista_Vasca" title="Accin Nacionalista Vasca">
       Accin Nacionalista Vasca
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Basque_Lands" title="Communist Party of the Basque Lands">
       Communist Party of the Basque Lands
      </a>
      (EHAK/PCTV,
      <i>
       Euskal Herrialdeetako Alderdi Komunista/Partido Comunista de las Tierras Vascas
      </i>
      ) were declared illegal in September 2008.
     </p>
     <p>
      A new party called
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aukera_Guztiak" title="Aukera Guztiak">
       Aukera Guztiak
      </a>
      <i>
       (All the Options)
      </i>
      was formed expressly for the elections to the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_Parliament" title="Basque Parliament">
       Basque Parliament
      </a>
      of April 2005. Its supporters claimed no heritage from Batasuna, asserting that their aim was to allow Basque citizens to freely express their political ideas, even those of independence. On the matter of political violence, Aukera Guztiak stated their right not to condemn some kinds of violence more than others if they did not see fit (in this regard, the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_National_Liberation_Movement" title="Basque National Liberation Movement">
       Basque National Liberation Movement
      </a>
      (MLNV) regards present police actions as violence, torture and state terrorism). Nevertheless, most of their members and certainly most of their leadership were former Batasuna supporters or affiliates. The Spanish Supreme Court unanimously considered the party to be a sequel to Batasuna and declared a ban on it.
     </p>
     <p>
      After Aukera Guztiak had been banned, and less than two weeks before the election, another political group appeared born from an earlier schism from Herri Batasuna, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_the_Basque_Lands" title="Communist Party of the Basque Lands">
       Communist Party of the Basque Lands
      </a>
      (EHAK/PCTV,
      <i>
       Euskal Herrialdeetako Alderdi Komunista/Partido Comunista de las Tierras Vascas
      </i>
      ), a formerly unknown political party which had no representation in the Autonomous Basque Parliament. EHAK made the announcement that they would apply the votes they obtained to sustain the political programme of the now banned Aukera Guztiak platform.
     </p>
     <p>
      This move left no time for the Spanish courts to investigate EHAK in compliance with the
      <i>
       Ley de Partidos
      </i>
      before the elections were held. The bulk of Batasuna supporters voted in this election for PCTV, a virtually unknown political formation until then. PCTV obtained 9 seats of 75 (12.44% of votes) at the Basque Parliament.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The election of EHAK representatives eventually allowed the programme of the now-illegal Batasuna to continue being represented without having condemned violence as required by the
      <i>
       Ley de Partidos
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      In February 2011, Sortu, a party described as "the new Batasuna",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LV8F_38-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-LV8F-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was launched. Unlike predecessor parties, Sortu explicitly rejects politically motivated violence, including that of ETA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LV8F_38-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-LV8F-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, on 23 March 2011, the Spanish Supreme Court banned Sortu from registering as a political party on the grounds that it was linked to ETA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Social_support">
       Social support
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Social support">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ETA_Pasajes_2003_06_28.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="700" data-file-width="525" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ETA_Pasajes_2003_06_28.jpg/220px-ETA_Pasajes_2003_06_28.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ETA_Pasajes_2003_06_28.jpg/330px-ETA_Pasajes_2003_06_28.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/ETA_Pasajes_2003_06_28.jpg/440px-ETA_Pasajes_2003_06_28.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ETA_Pasajes_2003_06_28.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Graffiti in
        <a href="/wiki/Pasaia" title="Pasaia">
         Pasaia
        </a>
        (2003). "ETA, the people with you" on the left, and Batasuna using several nationalist symbols asking for "Independence!"
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">
       Spanish transition to democracy
      </a>
      from 1975 on and ETA's progressive radicalisation have resulted in a steady loss of support, which became especially apparent at the time of their 1997 kidnapping and countdown assassination of
      <a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Blanco" title="Miguel ngel Blanco">
       Miguel ngel Blanco
      </a>
      . Their loss of sympathisers has been reflected in an erosion of support for the political parties identified with them. In the 1998 Basque parliament elections Euskal Herritarrok, formerly Batasuna, polled 17.7% of the votes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
       <a href="#cite_note-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, by 2001 the party's support had fallen to 10.0%.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
       <a href="#cite_note-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      There were also concerns that Spain's "judicial offensive" against alleged ETA supporters (two Basque political parties and one NGO were banned in September 2008) constitute a threat to human rights. Strong evidence was seen that a legal network had grown so wide as to lead to the arrest of numerous innocent people. According to
      <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">
       Amnesty International
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">
       torture
      </a>
      was still "persistent", though not "systematic." Inroads could be undermined by judicial short-cuts and abuses of human rights.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
       <a href="#cite_note-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Opinion_polls">
       Opinion polls
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Opinion polls">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euskobarometro" title="Euskobarometro">
       Euskobarometro
      </a>
      , the survey carried out by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_del_Pa%C3%ADs_Vasco" title="Universidad del Pas Vasco">
       Universidad del Pas Vasco
      </a>
      (University of the Basque Country), asking about the views of ETA within the Basque population, obtained these results in May 2009:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Euskobarometro_43-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Euskobarometro-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      64% rejected ETA totally, 13% identified themselves as former ETA sympathisers (mainly during the Franco dictatorship) who no longer support the group. Another 10% agreed with ETA's ends, but not their means. 3% said that their attitude towards ETA was mainly one of fear, 3% expressed indifference and 3% were undecided or did not answer. About 3% gave ETA "justified, with criticism" support (supporting the group but criticising some of their actions) and only 1% gave ETA total support. Even within Batasuna voters, at least 48% rejected ETA's violence.
     </p>
     <p>
      A poll taken by the Basque Autonomous Government in December 2006 during ETA's
      <a href="/wiki/ETA%27s_2006_ceasefire_declaration" title="ETA's 2006 ceasefire declaration">
       "permanent" ceasefire
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      showed that 88% of the Basques thought that it was necessary for all political parties to launch a dialogue, including a debate on the political framework for the Basque Country (86%). 69% support the idea of ratifying the results of this hypothetical multiparty dialogue through a referendum. This poll also reveals that the hope of a peaceful resolution to the issue of the constitutional status of the Basque region has fallen to 78% (from 90% in April).
     </p>
     <p>
      These polls did not cover
      <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">
       Navarre
      </a>
      , where support for Basque nationalist electoral options is weaker (around 25% of population) or the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Basque_Country" title="Northern Basque Country">
       Northern Basque Country
      </a>
      where support is even weaker (around 15% of population).
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="During_Franco.27s_dictatorship">
       During Franco's dictatorship
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: During Franco's dictatorship">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      ETA grew from a student group called Ekin, founded in the early 1950s, which published a magazine and undertook direct action.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-newandcourrier_46-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-newandcourrier-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ETA was founded on 31 July 1959 as Euskadi Ta Askatasuna (Basque Homeland and Freedom) by students frustrated by the moderate stance of the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_Nationalist_Party" title="Basque Nationalist Party">
       Basque Nationalist Party
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studentgroup_47-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-studentgroup-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      (Originally, the name for the organisation used the word
      <i>
       Aberri
      </i>
      instead of
      <i>
       Euskadi
      </i>
      , creating the acronym
      <i>
       ATA
      </i>
      . However, in some Basque dialects,
      <i>
       ata
      </i>
      means
      <i>
       duck
      </i>
      , so the name was changed.)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kurlansky-2004_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Kurlansky-2004-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA held their first assembly in
      <a href="/wiki/Bayonne" title="Bayonne">
       Bayonne
      </a>
      , France, in 1962, during which a "declaration of principles" was formulated and following which a structure of activist cells was developed.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conversi_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Conversi-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Subsequently,
      <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">
       Marxist
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third-worldist" title="Third-worldist">
       third-worldist
      </a>
      perspectives developed within ETA, becoming the basis for a political programme set out in Federico Krutwig's 1963 book
      <i>
       Vasconia
      </i>
      , which is considered to be the defining text of the movement. In contrast to previous Basque nationalist platforms, Krutwig's vision was anti-religious and based upon language and culture rather than race.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conversi_49-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Conversi-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ETA's third and fourth assemblies, held in 1964 and 1965, adopted an anti-capitalist and anti-imperialist position, seeing nationalism and the class struggle as intrinsically connected.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conversi_49-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Conversi-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Placa_Carrero_Blanco.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="615" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Placa_Carrero_Blanco.jpg/220px-Placa_Carrero_Blanco.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Placa_Carrero_Blanco.jpg/330px-Placa_Carrero_Blanco.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Placa_Carrero_Blanco.jpg/440px-Placa_Carrero_Blanco.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Placa_Carrero_Blanco.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Memorial plate at the place of the assassination of Admiral
        <a href="/wiki/Luis_Carrero_Blanco" title="Luis Carrero Blanco">
         Luis Carrero Blanco
        </a>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Some sources attribute the 1960 bombing of the Amara station in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donostia-San_Sebastian" title="Donostia-San Sebastian">
       Donostia-San Sebastian
      </a>
      (which killed a 22-month-old child) to ETA,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
       <a href="#cite_note-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_51-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EC-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but statistics published by the
      <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_the_Interior_(Spain)" title="Ministry of the Interior (Spain)">
       Spanish Ministry of the Interior
      </a>
      have always showed that ETA's first victim was killed in 1968.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SpainInteriorMinistryStatistics_52-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SpainInteriorMinistryStatistics-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 1960 attack was claimed by the Portuguese and Spanish left-wing group
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Directorio_Revolucionario_Ib%C3%A9rico_de_Liberaci%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Directorio Revolucionario Ibrico de Liberacin (page does not exist)">
       DRIL
      </a>
      (together with four other very similar bombings committed that same day across Spain, all of them attributed to DRIL
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deia-21feb2010_53-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-deia-21feb2010-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ), and the attribution to ETA has been considered to be unfounded by the researchers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EC_51-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-EC-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deia-21feb2010_53-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-deia-21feb2010-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
       <a href="#cite_note-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bego.C3.B1a_Urroz_afera_55-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Bego.C3.B1a_Urroz_afera-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      And police documents dating from 1961, released in 2013, show that the DRIL was indeed the author of the bombing.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA's first killing occurred on 7 June 1968, when
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guardia_Civil_(Spain)" title="Guardia Civil (Spain)">
       Guardia Civil
      </a>
      member Jos Pardines Arcay was shot dead after he tried to halt ETA member
      <a href="/wiki/Txabi_Etxebarrieta" title="Txabi Etxebarrieta">
       Txabi Etxebarrieta
      </a>
      during a routine road check. Etxebarrieta was chased down and killed as he tried to flee.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This led to retaliation in the form of the first planned ETA assassination: that of
      <a href="/wiki/Melit%C3%B3n_Manzanas" title="Melitn Manzanas">
       Melitn Manzanas
      </a>
      , chief of the
      <a href="/wiki/Secret_police" title="Secret police">
       secret police
      </a>
      in San Sebastin and associated with a long record of tortures inflicted on detainees in his custody.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In December 1970, several members of ETA were condemned to death in the
      <i>
       Proceso de Burgos
      </i>
      ("
      <a href="/wiki/Burgos" title="Burgos">
       Burgos
      </a>
      Trial"), but international pressure resulted in their sentences being
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commutation_(law)" title="Commutation (law)">
       commuted
      </a>
      (a process which, however, had by that time already been applied to some other members of ETA).
     </p>
     <p>
      In early December 1970, ETA kidnapped the German consul in San Sebastian, Eugen Beilh, in order to exchange him for the Burgos defendants. He was released unharmed on 24 December.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Nationalists who refused to follow the tenets of MarxismLeninism and who sought to create a
      <a href="/wiki/United_front" title="United front">
       united front
      </a>
      appeared as ETA-V, but lacked the support to challenge ETA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sullivan_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sullivan-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The most significant assassination performed by ETA during Franco's dictatorship was
      <a href="/wiki/Operaci%C3%B3n_Ogro" title="Operacin Ogro">
       Operacin Ogro
      </a>
      , the December 1973 bomb assassination in
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
       Madrid
      </a>
      of Admiral
      <a href="/wiki/Luis_Carrero_Blanco" title="Luis Carrero Blanco">
       Luis Carrero Blanco
      </a>
      , Franco's chosen successor and president of the government (a position roughly equivalent to being a prime minister). The assassination had been planned for months and was executed by placing a bomb in the sewer below the street where Carrero Blanco's car passed every day. The bomb blew up beneath the politician's car and threw it five stories into the air and over the top of a nearby building onto a balcony in a nearby courtyard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-studentgroup_47-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-studentgroup-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      For some in the Spanish opposition, Carrero Blanco's assassination i.e. the elimination of Franco's chosen successor was an instrumental step for the subsequent establishment of democracy.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2011)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="During_the_transition">
       During the transition
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: During the transition">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      During the
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">
       Spanish transition to democracy
      </a>
      which began following Franco's death, ETA split into two separate groups:
      <a href="/wiki/ETA_political-military" title="ETA political-military">
       ETA political-military
      </a>
      or ETA(pm), and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ETA_military" title="ETA military">
       ETA military
      </a>
      or ETA(m).
     </p>
     <p>
      Both ETA(m) and ETA(pm) refused offers of amnesty, and instead pursued and intensified their violent struggle. The years 197880 were to prove ETA's most deadly, with 68, 76, and 98 fatalities, respectively. [Martinez-Herrera 2002]
     </p>
     <p>
      During the Franco dictatorship, ETA was able to take advantage of tolerance by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_government" title="French government">
       French government
      </a>
      , which allowed its members to move freely through French territory, believing that in this manner they were contributing to the end of Franco's regime. There is much controversy over the degree to which this policy of "
      <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary" title="Sanctuary">
       sanctuary
      </a>
      " continued even after the transition to democracy, but it is generally agreed that currently the French authorities collaborate closely with the Spanish government against ETA.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the 1980s, ETA(pm) accepted the Spanish government's offer of individual pardons to all ETA prisoners, even those who had committed violent crimes, who publicly abandoned the policy of violence. This caused a new division in ETA(pm) between the seventh and eighth assemblies. ETA VII accepted this partial amnesty granted by the now democratic Spanish government and integrated into the political party
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Euskadiko_Ezkerra" title="Euskadiko Ezkerra">
        Euskadiko Ezkerra
       </a>
      </i>
      ("
      <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">
       Left
      </a>
      of the Basque Country").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA VIII, after a brief period of independent activity, eventually integrated into ETA(m). With no factions existing anymore, ETA(m) revamped the original name of Euskadi Ta Askatasuna.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="GAL">
       GAL
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: GAL">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      During the 1980s a "dirty war" ensued by means of the
      <a href="/wiki/Grupos_Antiterroristas_de_Liberaci%C3%B3n" title="Grupos Antiterroristas de Liberacin">
       Grupos Antiterroristas de Liberacin
      </a>
      (GAL, "Antiterrorist Liberation Groups"), a paramilitary group which billed themselves as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counter-terrorist" title="Counter-terrorist">
       counter-terrorist
      </a>
      , active between 1983 and 1987. The GAL committed assassinations, kidnappings and torture, not only of ETA members but of civilians supposedly related to those, some of whom turned out to have nothing to do with ETA. 27 people were killed by GAL.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamaria437_62-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-santamaria437-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      GAL activities were a follow-up of similar dirty war actions by death squads, actively supported by members of Spanish security forces and secret services, using names such as
      <a href="/wiki/Batall%C3%B3n_Vasco_Espa%C3%B1ol" title="Batalln Vasco Espaol">
       Batalln Vasco Espaol
      </a>
      active from 1975 to 1981. They were responsible for the killing of about 48 people.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-santamaria437_62-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-santamaria437-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      One consequence of GAL's activities in France was the decision in 1984 by interior minister Pierre Joxe to permit the extradition of ETA suspects to Spain. Reaching this decision had taken 25 years and was critical in curbing ETA's capabilities by denial of previously safe territory in France.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The airing of the state-sponsored "dirty war" scheme and the imprisonment of officials responsible for GAL in the early 1990s led to a political scandal in Spain. The group's connections with the state were unveiled by the Spanish journal
      <a href="/wiki/El_Mundo_(Spain)" title="El Mundo (Spain)">
       El Mundo
      </a>
      , with an
      <a href="/wiki/Investigative_journalism" title="Investigative journalism">
       investigative
      </a>
      series leading to the GAL plot being discovered and a national trial initiated. As a consequence, the group's attacks since the revelation have generally been dubbed
      <a href="/wiki/State_terrorism" title="State terrorism">
       state terrorism
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1997 the Spanish
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audiencia_Nacional" title="Audiencia Nacional">
       Audiencia Nacional
      </a>
      court finished its trial, which resulted in convictions and imprisonment of several individuals related to the GAL, including civil servants up to the highest levels of the
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">
       Spanish Socialist Workers' Party
      </a>
      (PSOE) government, such as former Homeland Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Barrionuevo" title="Jos Barrionuevo">
       Jos Barrionuevo
      </a>
      . Premier
      <a href="/wiki/Felipe_Gonz%C3%A1lez" title="Felipe Gonzlez">
       Felipe Gonzlez
      </a>
      was quoted as saying that the
      <a href="/wiki/Rechtsstaat" title="Rechtsstaat">
       constitutional state
      </a>
      has to defend itself "also in the sewers" (
      <i>
       El Estado de derecho tambin se defiende en las cloacas
      </i>
      ) something which, for some, indicated at least his knowledge of the scheme. However, his involvement with the GAL could never be proven.
     </p>
     <p>
      These events marked the end of the armed "counter-terrorist" period in Spain and no major cases of foul play on the part of the Spanish government after 1987 (when GAL ceased to operate) have been proven in courts.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">
       Human rights
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Human rights">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      According to the radical nationalist group, Euskal Memoria, between 1960 and 2010 there were 465 deaths in the Basque Country due to (primarily Spanish) "state violence".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This figure is considerably higher than those given elsewhere, which are usually between 250 and 300.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Critics of ETA cite only 56 members of that organisation killed by state forces since 1975.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA members and supporters routinely claim
      <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">
       torture
      </a>
      at the hands of Spanish police forces.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publico_68-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-publico-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While these claims are hard to verify, some convictions are based on confessions while prisoners are held
      <i>
       incomunicado
      </i>
      and without access to a lawyer of their choice, for a maximum of five days. These confessions are routinely repudiated by the defendants during trials as having been extracted under torture. There have been some successful prosecutions of proven tortures during the "dirty war" period of the mid-1980s, although the penalties have been considered by
      <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">
       Amnesty International
      </a>
      as unjustifiably light and lenient with co-conspirators and enablers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIUN2002_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-AIUN2002-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AIUN2002Update_70-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-AIUN2002Update-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In this regard, Amnesty International has shown concern for the continuous disregard on the recommendations issued by the agency to prevent the alleged abuses to possibly take place.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
       <a href="#cite_note-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Also in this regard, ETA's manuals have been found instructing its members and supporters to claim routinely that they had been tortured while detained.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-publico_68-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-publico-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Unai Romano's case has been very controversial. Pictures of him with a symmetrically swollen face of uncertain etiology were published after his incommunicado period leading to claims of police abuse and torture. Martxelo Otamendi, the ex-director of the Basque newspaper Euskaldunon Egunkaria, decided to bring charges in September 2008 against the Spanish Government in Strasbourg Court for "not inspecting properly" torture denounced cases.
     </p>
     <p>
      As a result of ETA's violence, threats and killings of journalists,
      <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">
       Reporters Without Borders
      </a>
      has included Spain in all six editions of its annual watchlist on
      <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_press" title="Freedom of the press">
       press freedom
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
       <a href="#cite_note-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Thus, this NGO has included ETA in its watchlist "Predators of Press Freedom".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
       <a href="#cite_note-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Under_democracy">
       Under democracy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Under democracy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      ETA performed their first
      <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">
       car bomb
      </a>
      assassination in
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
       Madrid
      </a>
      in September 1985, resulting in one death (American citizen Eugene Kent Brown, Johnson &amp; Johnson employee) and sixteen injuries; the
      <a href="/wiki/Plaza_Rep%C3%BAblica_Dominicana_bombing" title="Plaza Repblica Dominicana bombing">
       Plaza Repblica Dominicana bombing
      </a>
      in July 1986 killed 12 members of the Guardia Civil and injured 50; on 19 June 1987, the
      <a href="/wiki/1987_Hipercor_bombing" title="1987 Hipercor bombing">
       Hipercor bombing
      </a>
      was an attack in a shopping center in
      <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">
       Barcelona
      </a>
      , killing twenty-one and injuring forty-five; in the last case, entire families were killed. The horror caused then was so striking that ETA felt compelled to issue a communiqu stating that they had given warning of the Hipercor bomb, but that the police had declined to evacuate the area. The police claim that the warning came only a few minutes before the bomb exploded.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1986
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gesto_por_la_Paz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gesto por la Paz (page does not exist)">
       Gesto por la Paz
      </a>
      (known in English as
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Association_for_Peace_in_the_Basque_Country&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Association for Peace in the Basque Country (page does not exist)">
       Association for Peace in the Basque Country
      </a>
      ) was founded; they began to convene silent demonstrations in communities throughout the Basque Country the day after any violent killing, whether by ETA or by GAL. These were the first systematic demonstrations in the Basque Country against political violence. Also in 1986, in
      <a href="/wiki/Ordizia" title="Ordizia">
       Ordizia
      </a>
      , ETA shot down
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mar%C3%ADa_Dolores_Katarain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mara Dolores Katarain (page does not exist)">
       Mara Dolores Katarain
      </a>
      , known as "Yoyes", while she was walking with her infant son. Yoyes was a former member of ETA who had abandoned the armed struggle and rejoined civil society: they accused her of "desertion" because of her taking advantage of the Spanish reinsertion policy which granted amnesty to those prisoners who publicly refused political violence (see below).
     </p>
     <p>
      On 12 January 1988, all Basque political parties except ETA-affiliated
      <a href="/wiki/Batasuna" title="Batasuna">
       Herri Batasuna
      </a>
      signed the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ajuria-Enea_pact&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ajuria-Enea pact (page does not exist)">
       Ajuria-Enea pact
      </a>
      with the intent of ending ETA's violence. Weeks later on 28 January, ETA announced a 60-day "ceasefire", later prolonged several times. Negotiations known as the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mesa_de_Argel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mesa de Argel (page does not exist)">
       Mesa de Argel
      </a>
      ("
      <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">
       Algiers
      </a>
      Table") took place between the ETA representative
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Eugenio_Etxebeste&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Eugenio Etxebeste (page does not exist)">
       Eugenio Etxebeste
      </a>
      ("Antxon"), and the then PSOE government of Spain but no successful conclusion was reached, and ETA eventually resumed the use of violence.
     </p>
     <p>
      During this period, the Spanish government had a policy referred to as "
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Reinsertion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Reinsertion (page does not exist)">
       reinsertion
      </a>
      ", under which imprisoned ETA members whom the government believed had genuinely abandoned violence could be freed and allowed to rejoin society. Claiming a need to prevent ETA from coercively impeding this reinsertion, the PSOE government decided that imprisoned ETA members, who previously had all been imprisoned within the Basque Country, would instead be dispersed to prisons throughout Spain, some as far from their families as in the
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Salto_del_Negro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Salto del Negro (page does not exist)">
       Salto del Negro
      </a>
      prison in the
      <a href="/wiki/Canary_Islands" title="Canary Islands">
       Canary Islands
      </a>
      . France has taken a similar approach.
     </p>
     <p>
      In the event, the only clear effect of this policy was to incite social protest, especially from nationalists and families of the prisoners, claiming cruelty of separating family members from the insurgents. Much of the protest against this policy runs under the slogan "
      <i>
       Euskal Presoak  Euskal Herrira
      </i>
      " (
      <i>
       Basque prisoners to the Basque Country
      </i>
      , by "Basque prisoners" only ETA members are meant). It has to be noted that almost in any Spanish jail there is a group of ETA prisoners, as the number of ETA prisoners makes it difficult to disperse them.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EPPK_2008.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="704" data-file-width="1024" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/EPPK_2008.jpg/220px-EPPK_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/EPPK_2008.jpg/330px-EPPK_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/EPPK_2008.jpg/440px-EPPK_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EPPK_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Banner in support of imprisoned ETA members, by
        <i>
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gestoras_pro-Amnist%C3%ADa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gestoras pro-Amnista (page does not exist)">
          Gestoras pro-Amnista
         </a>
         /
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Amnistiaren_Aldeko_Batzordeak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Amnistiaren Aldeko Batzordeak (page does not exist)">
          Amnistiaren Aldeko Batzordeak
         </a>
        </i>
        ("Pro-Amnesty Managing Assemblies", currently illegal)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      <i>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gestoras_pro-Amnist%C3%ADa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gestoras pro-Amnista (page does not exist)">
        Gestoras pro-Amnista
       </a>
       /
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Amnistiaren_Aldeko_Batzordeak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Amnistiaren Aldeko Batzordeak (page does not exist)">
        Amnistiaren Aldeko Batzordeak
       </a>
      </i>
      ("Pro-Amnesty Managing Assemblies", currently illegal), later
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Askatasuna" title="Askatasuna">
        Askatasuna
       </a>
      </i>
      ("Freedom") and
      <i>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Senideak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Senideak (page does not exist)">
        Senideak
       </a>
      </i>
      ("The family members") provided support for prisoners and families. The
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_Government" title="Basque Government">
       Basque Government
      </a>
      and several Nationalist town halls granted money on humanitarian reasons for relatives to visit prisoners. The long road trips have caused accidental deaths that are protested against by Nationalist Prisoner's Family supporters.
     </p>
     <p>
      During the ETA ceasefire of the late 1990s, the PSOE government brought back to the mainland the prisoners on the islands and in Africa.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2007)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      Since the end of the ceasefire, ETA prisoners have not been sent back to overseas prisons. Some Basque authorities have established grants for the expenses of visiting families.
     </p>
     <p>
      Another Spanish "counter-terrorist" law puts suspected terrorist cases under the central tribunal
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Audiencia_Nacional" title="Audiencia Nacional">
        Audiencia Nacional
       </a>
      </i>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
       Madrid
      </a>
      , due to the threats by the group over the Basque courts. Under Article 509 suspected terrorists are subject to being held "incommunicado" for up to thirteen days, during which they have no contact with the outside world other than through the court appointed lawyer, including informing their family of their arrest, consultation with private lawyers or examination by a physician other than the
      <a href="/wiki/Coroner" title="Coroner">
       coroners
      </a>
      . In comparison, the
      <a href="/wiki/Habeas_corpus" title="Habeas corpus">
       habeas corpus
      </a>
      term for other suspects is three days.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1992, ETA's three top leaders"military" leader
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Francisco_Mujika_Garmendia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Francisco Mujika Garmendia (page does not exist)">
       Francisco Mujika Garmendia
      </a>
      ("Pakito"), political leader
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Alvarez_Santacristina&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jos Luis Alvarez Santacristina (page does not exist)">
       Jos Luis Alvarez Santacristina
      </a>
      ("Txelis") and logistical leader
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Arregi_Erostarbe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jos Mara Arregi Erostarbe (page does not exist)">
       Jos Mara Arregi Erostarbe
      </a>
      ("Fiti"), often referred to collectively as the "cpula" of ETA or as the Artapalo collective
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
       <a href="#cite_note-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      were arrested in the northern Basque town of
      <a href="/wiki/Bidart" title="Bidart">
       Bidart
      </a>
      , which led to changes in ETA's leadership and direction.
     </p>
     <p>
      After a two-month truce, ETA adopted even more radical positions. The principal consequence of the change appears to have been the creation of the "
      <i>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Y_Groups&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Y Groups (page does not exist)">
        Y Groups
       </a>
      </i>
      ", formed by young militants of ETA parallel groups (generally
      <a href="/wiki/Minor_(law)" title="Minor (law)">
       minors
      </a>
      ), dedicated to so-called "
      <i>
       kale borroka
      </i>
      "street struggleand whose activities included burning buses, street lamps, benches,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Automatic_teller_machine" title="Automatic teller machine">
       ATMs
      </a>
      , garbage containers, and throwing
      <a href="/wiki/Molotov_cocktail" title="Molotov cocktail">
       Molotov cocktails
      </a>
      . The appearance of these groups was attributed by many to the supposed weakness of ETA, which obliged them to resort to minors to maintain or augment their impact on society after arrests of leading militants, including the "cupola". ETA also began to menace leaders of other parties besides rival Basque nationalist parties.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1995, the armed group again launched a peace proposal. The so-called "Democratic Alternative" replaced the earlier
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Koordinadora_Abertzale_Sozialista&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Koordinadora Abertzale Sozialista (page does not exist)">
       KAS
      </a>
      Alternative as a minimum proposal for the establishment of Euskal Herria. The Democratic Alternative offered the cessation of all armed ETA activity if the Spanish-government would recognize the Basque people as having sovereignty over Basque territory, the right to
      <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">
       self-determination
      </a>
      and that it freed all ETA members in prison. The Spanish government ultimately rejected this peace offer as it would go against the
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Constitution_of_1978" title="Spanish Constitution of 1978">
       Spanish Constitution of 1978
      </a>
      . Changing the constitution was not considered.
     </p>
     <p>
      Also in 1995 came a failed ETA car bombing attempt directed against
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="Jos Mara Aznar">
       Jos Mara Aznar
      </a>
      , a conservative politician who was leader of the then-opposition
      <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">
       Partido Popular
      </a>
      (PP) and was shortly after elected to the presidency of the government; there was also an abortive attempt in
      <a href="/wiki/Majorca" title="Majorca">
       Majorca
      </a>
      on the life of King
      <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_I_of_Spain" title="Juan Carlos I of Spain">
       Juan CarlosI
      </a>
      . Still, the act with the largest social impact came the following year. 10 July 1997, PP council member
      <a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Blanco" title="Miguel ngel Blanco">
       Miguel ngel Blanco
      </a>
      was kidnapped in the Basque town of
      <a href="/wiki/Ermua" title="Ermua">
       Ermua
      </a>
      , with the separatist group threatening to assassinate him unless the Spanish government met ETA's demand of starting to bring all ETA's inmates to prisons of the Basque Country within two days after the kidnapping.
     </p>
     <p>
      This demand was not met by the Spanish government and after three days Miguel ngel Blanco was found shot dead when the deadline expired. More than six million people took out to the streets to demand his liberation, with massive demonstrations occurring as much in the Basque regions as elsewhere in Spain, chanting cries of "Assassins" and "Basques yes, ETA no". This response came to be known as the "Spirit of Ermua".
     </p>
     <p>
      Later came acts of violence such as the 6 November 2001 car bomb in Madrid which injured 65 people, and attacks on
      <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
       football
      </a>
      stadiums and tourist destinations throughout Spain.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/11_September_2001_attacks" title="11 September 2001 attacks">
       11 September 2001 attacks
      </a>
      in the USA appeared to have dealt a hard blow to ETA, owing to the worldwide toughening of "anti-terrorist" measures (such as the freezing of bank accounts), the increase in international police coordination, and the end of the toleration some countries had, up until then, extended to ETA. In addition, in 2002 the Basque nationalist youth movement,
      <i>
       Jarrai
      </i>
      , was outlawed and the law of parties was changed outlawing Herri Batasuna, the "political arm" of ETA (although even before the change in law, Batasuna had been largely paralysed and under judicial investigation by judge
      <a href="/wiki/Baltasar_Garz%C3%B3n" title="Baltasar Garzn">
       Baltasar Garzn
      </a>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      With ever-increasing frequency, attempted ETA actions have been frustrated by Spanish security forces.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 24 December 2003, in San Sebastin and in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hernani,_Spain" title="Hernani, Spain">
       Hernani
      </a>
      , National Police arrested two ETA members who had left dynamite in a railroad car prepared to explode in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chamart%C3%ADn_Station" title="Chamartn Station">
       Chamartn Station
      </a>
      in Madrid. On 1 March 2004, in a place between
      <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcal de Henares">
       Alcal de Henares
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
       Madrid
      </a>
      , a light truck with 536kg of explosives was discovered by the Guardia Civil.
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA was initially blamed for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/11_March_2004_Madrid_train_bombings" title="11 March 2004 Madrid train bombings">
       2004 Madrid bombings
      </a>
      by the outgoing government
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and large sections of the press.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
