        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the group denied responsibility and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic_fundamentalists" title="Islamic fundamentalists">
       Islamic fundamentalists
      </a>
      from Morocco were eventually convicted. The judicial investigation currently states that there is no relationship between ETA and the Madrid bombings.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2006_ceasefire_declaration">
       2006 ceasefire declaration
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2006 ceasefire declaration">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atentado_de_ETA_en_el_aeropuerto_de_Madrid_Barajas4.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Atentado_de_ETA_en_el_aeropuerto_de_Madrid_Barajas4.jpg/220px-Atentado_de_ETA_en_el_aeropuerto_de_Madrid_Barajas4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Atentado_de_ETA_en_el_aeropuerto_de_Madrid_Barajas4.jpg/330px-Atentado_de_ETA_en_el_aeropuerto_de_Madrid_Barajas4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Atentado_de_ETA_en_el_aeropuerto_de_Madrid_Barajas4.jpg/440px-Atentado_de_ETA_en_el_aeropuerto_de_Madrid_Barajas4.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atentado_de_ETA_en_el_aeropuerto_de_Madrid_Barajas4.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Barajas Airport parking lot after the bomb
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ETA%27s_2006_%22permanent_ceasefire%22" title="ETA's 2006 &quot;permanent ceasefire&quot;">
       ETA's 2006 "permanent ceasefire"
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Madrid_Barajas_International_Airport_bombing" title="2006 Madrid Barajas International Airport bombing">
       2006 Madrid Barajas International Airport bombing
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the context of negotiation with the Spanish government, ETA has declared what it has described as "truce" a number of times since its creation.
     </p>
     <p>
      On 22 March 2006, ETA sent a DVD message to the Basque Network
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euskal_Irrati-Telebista" title="Euskal Irrati-Telebista">
       Euskal Irrati-Telebista
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
       <a href="#cite_note-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the journals
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Gara" title="Gara">
        Gara
       </a>
      </i>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Berria" title="Berria">
       Berria
      </a>
      with a communiqu from the group announcing what it called a "permanent ceasefire" that was broadcast over Spanish TV.
     </p>
     <p>
      Talks with the group were then officially opened by Spanish
      <i>
       Presidente del Gobierno
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="Jos Luis Rodrguez Zapatero">
       Jos Luis Rodrguez Zapatero
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      These took place all over 2006, not free from incidents such as an ETA cell stealing some 300 handguns, ammunition and spare parts in France on October 2006.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      or a series of warnings made by ETA such as the one of 23 September, when masked ETA militants declared that the group would "keep taking up arms" until achieving "independence and socialism in the Basque country",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
       <a href="#cite_note-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which were regarded by some as a way to increase pressure on the talks, by others as a tactic to reinforce ETA's position in the negotiations.
     </p>
     <p>
      Finally, on
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2006_Madrid_Barajas_International_Airport_bombing" title="2006 Madrid Barajas International Airport bombing">
       30 December 2006 ETA detonated a van bomb
      </a>
      after three confusing warning calls, in a parking building at the
      <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
       Madrid
      </a>
      Barajas international airport. The explosion caused the collapse of the building and killed two Ecuadorian immigrants who were napping inside their cars in the parking building.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
       <a href="#cite_note-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At
      <span class="nowrap">
       6:00pm
      </span>
      , Jos Luis Rodrguez Zapatero released a statement stating that the "peace process" had been discontinued.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Current_events">
       Current events
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Current events">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_ETA_attacks" title="List of ETA attacks">
       List of ETA attacks
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In January 2008, ETA stated that its call for independence is similar to that of the
      <a href="/wiki/Kosovo_status_process" title="Kosovo status process">
       Kosovo status
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">
       Scotland
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
       <a href="#cite_note-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In the week of 8 September 2008, two Basque political parties were banned by a Spanish court for their secretive links to ETA. In another case in the same week, 21 people were convicted whose work on behalf of ETA prisoners actually belied secretive links to the armed separatists themselves.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2008)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      ETA reacted to these actions by placing three major car bombs in less than 24 hours in northern Spain.
     </p>
     <p>
      In April 2009
      <a href="/wiki/Jurdan_Martitegi" title="Jurdan Martitegi">
       Jurdan Martitegi
      </a>
      was arrested, making the fourth consecutive ETA military chiefs to be captured within a single year, an unprecedented police record further weakening the group.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_84-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The group, and therefore the violence surged in summer 2009, with several ETA attacks leaving three people dead and dozens injured around Spain.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Basque newspaper
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Gara" title="Gara">
        Gara
       </a>
      </i>
      published an article that suggested that ETA member Jon Anza could have been killed and buried by Spanish police in April 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The central prosecutor in the French town of Bayonne, Anne Kayanakis, announced, as the official version, that the autopsy carried out on the body of Jon Anza  a suspected member of the armed Basque group ETA, missing since April 2009  revealed no signs of having been beaten, wounded or shot, which should rule out any suspicions that he died from unnatural causes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eitb.com_86-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-eitb.com-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Nevertheless, that very magistrate denied the demand of the family asking for the presence of a family doctor during the autopsy. After this Jon Anza's family members asked for a second autopsy to be carried on.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gara.net_87-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gara.net-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In December 2009, Spain raised its terror alert after warning that ETA could be planning major attacks or high-profile kidnappings during Spain's European Union presidency. The next day, after being asked by the opposition,
      <a href="/wiki/Alfredo_P%C3%A9rez_Rubalcaba" title="Alfredo Prez Rubalcaba">
       Alfredo Prez Rubalcaba
      </a>
      said that warning was part of a strategy.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2010_ceasefire">
       2010 ceasefire
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2010 ceasefire">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On 5 September 2010, ETA declared a new ceasefire, its third, after two previous ceasefires were ended by the group. A spokesperson speaking on a video announcing the ceasefire said the group wished to use "peaceful, democratic means" to achieve its aims, though it was not specified whether the ceasefire was considered permanent by the group. ETA claimed that it had made the decision to initiate a ceasefire several months prior to the announcement. In part of the video, the spokesperson said that the group was "prepared today as yesterday to agree to the minimum democratic conditions necessary to put in motion a democratic process, if the Spanish government is willing."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_5_sep_20-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-bbc_5_sep-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The announcement was met with a mixed reaction; Basque nationalist politicians responded positively, and said that the Spanish and international governments should do the same, while the Spanish interior counselor of Basque, Rodolfo Ares, said that the commitment did not go far enough. He said that he considered ETA's statement "absolutely insufficient" because it did not commit to a complete termination of what Ares considered "terrorist activity" by the group.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc_5_sep_20-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-bbc_5_sep-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="2011_permanent_ceasefire_and_cessation_of_armed_activity">
       2011 permanent ceasefire and cessation of armed activity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2011 permanent ceasefire and cessation of armed activity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
       <div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:400px;" videopayload='&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="position:relative;display:block;width:768px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" style="width:768px;height:432px" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Konferentzia.ogv/768px--Konferentzia.ogv.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" class="kskin" data-durationhint="319.00734693878" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Konferentzia.ogv" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Konferentzia.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&quot;theora, vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file, 768  432 (2.1 Mbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="768" data-height="432" data-bandwidth="2098050" data-framerate="50" /&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/ff/Konferentzia.ogv/Konferentzia.ogv.160p.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&quot;theora, vorbis&quot;" transcodekey="160p.ogv" data-title="Low bandwidth Ogg video (160P)" data-shorttitle="Ogg 160P" data-width="284" data-height="160" data-bandwidth="193928" data-framerate="15" /&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/ff/Konferentzia.ogv/Konferentzia.ogv.360p.webm" type="video/webm; codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" transcodekey="360p.webm" data-title="Web streamable WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="537296" data-framerate="50" /&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/ff/Konferentzia.ogv/Konferentzia.ogv.360p.ogv" type="video/ogg; codecs=&quot;theora, vorbis&quot;" transcodekey="360p.ogv" data-title="Web streamable Ogg video (360P)" data-shorttitle="Ogg 360P" data-width="640" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="571544" data-framerate="50" /&gt;Sorry, your browser either has JavaScript disabled or does not have any supported player.&lt;br /&gt;
