        <img alt="File:Konferentzia.ogv" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Konferentzia.ogv/400px--Konferentzia.ogv.jpg" style="width:400px;height:225px"/>
        <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Konferentzia.ogv" target="new" title="Play media">
         <span class="play-btn-large">
          <span class="mw-tmh-playtext">
           Play media
          </span>
         </span>
        </a>
       </div>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Konferentzia.ogv" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The final declaration of the
        <a href="/wiki/Donostia-San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_International_Peace_Conference" title="Donostia-San Sebastin International Peace Conference">
         Donostia-San Sebastin International Peace Conference
        </a>
        (17 October 2011) led to an announcement of cessation of armed activity by ETA.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      On 10 January 2011, ETA declared that their September 2010 ceasefire would be permanent and verifiable by international observers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grauniad_88-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-grauniad-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Observers urged caution, pointing out that ETA had broken permanent ceasefires in the past,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grauniad_88-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-grauniad-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      whereas Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="Jos Luis Rodrguez Zapatero">
       Jos Luis Rodrguez Zapatero
      </a>
      (who left office in December 2011) demanded that ETA declare that it had given up violence for once and for all.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grauniad_88-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-grauniad-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the declaration, Spanish press started speculating of a possible
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_IRA" title="Real IRA">
       Real IRA
      </a>
      -type split within ETA, with hardliners forming a new more violent offshoot led by "Dienteputo".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
       <a href="#cite_note-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
       <a href="#cite_note-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 20 October 2011, ETA announced a cessation of armed activity via video clip sent to media outlets following the
      <a href="/wiki/Donostia-San_Sebasti%C3%A1n_International_Peace_Conference" title="Donostia-San Sebastin International Peace Conference">
       Donostia-San Sebastin International Peace Conference
      </a>
      , which was attended by former UN Secretary-General
      <a href="/wiki/Kofi_Annan" title="Kofi Annan">
       Kofi Annan
      </a>
      , former
      <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">
       Taoiseach
      </a>
      of Ireland
      <a href="/wiki/Bertie_Ahern" title="Bertie Ahern">
       Bertie Ahern
      </a>
      , former Prime Minister of Norway
      <a href="/wiki/Gro_Harlem_Brundtland" title="Gro Harlem Brundtland">
       Gro Harlem Brundtland
      </a>
      (an international leader in sustainable development and public health), former Interior Minister of France
      <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Joxe" title="Pierre Joxe">
       Pierre Joxe
      </a>
      , president of Sinn Fin
      <a href="/wiki/Gerry_Adams" title="Gerry Adams">
       Gerry Adams
      </a>
      (a
      <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta Dla">
       Teachta Dla
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="Dil ireann">
       Dil ireann
      </a>
      ), and British diplomat
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jonathan_Powell_(aide)" title="Jonathan Powell (aide)">
       Jonathan Powell
      </a>
      , who served as the first Downing Street Chief of Staff.
     </p>
     <p>
      They all signed a final declaration that was supported also by former UK Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Tony_Blair" title="Tony Blair">
       Tony Blair
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EITB20111017_92-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-EITB20111017-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the former US President and 2002 Nobel Peace Prize winner
      <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Carter" title="Jimmy Carter">
       Jimmy Carter
      </a>
      , and the former US senator and former US Special Envoy for Middle East Peace
      <a href="/wiki/George_J._Mitchell" title="George J. Mitchell">
       George J. Mitchell
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
       <a href="#cite_note-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The meeting did not include Spanish or French government representatives.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20Oct2011_CNN_Al_Goodman_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-20Oct2011_CNN_Al_Goodman-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The day after the ceasefire, in a contribution piece to the New York Times, Tony Blair indicated that lessons in dealing with paramilitary separatist groups can be learned from the way in which the Spanish administration handled ETA. Blair wrote, governments must firmly defend themselves, their principles and their people against terrorists. This requires good police and intelligence work as well as political determination. [However], firm security pressure on terrorists must be coupled with offering them a way out when they realize that they cannot win by violence. Terrorist groups are rarely defeated by military means alone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes1_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Blair also suggested that Spain will need to discuss weapon decommissioning, peace strategies, reparations for victims, and security with ETA, as Britain has discussed with the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provisional_IRA" title="Provisional IRA">
       Provisional IRA
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes1_95-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA has declared ceasefires many times before, most significantly in 1999 and 2006, but the Spanish government and media outlets have expressed particularly hopeful opinions regarding the permanence of this most recent proclamation. Spanish premier
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Zapatero" title="Jos Luis Rodrguez Zapatero">
       Jos Luis Rodrguez Zapatero
      </a>
      described the move as "a victory for democracy, law and reason".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC20111020_21-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-BBC20111020-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally, the effort of security and intelligence forces in Spain and France are cited by politicians as the primary instruments responsible for the weakening of ETA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
       <a href="#cite_note-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The optimism may come as a surprise considering ETAs failure to renounce the independence movement, which has been one of the Spanish governments requirements.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes2_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimes2-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In fact, ETAs ceasefire video ended with the assertion that the struggle for the Basque homeland continues.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtube1_98-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-youtube1-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Less optimistic, Spanish Prime Minister,
      <a href="/wiki/Mariano_Rajoy" title="Mariano Rajoy">
       Mariano Rajoy
      </a>
      , of the center-right
      <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">
       People's Party (Spain)
      </a>
      , expressed the need to push for the full dissolution of ETA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes2_97-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimes2-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The People's Party has emphasized the obligation of the state to refuse negotiations with separatist movements since former Prime Minister
      <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Aznar" title="Jos Mara Aznar">
       Jos Mara Aznar
      </a>
      was in office. Aznar was responsible for banning media outlets seen as subversive to the state and Batasuna, the political party of ETA.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
       <a href="#cite_note-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Additionally, in preparation for his partys manifesto, on 30 October 2011, Rajoy declared that the People's Party would not negotiate with ETA under threats of violence nor announcements of the groups termination, but would instead focus party efforts on remembering and honoring victims of separatist violence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100">
       <a href="#cite_note-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Significantly, while ETA pledged to refrain from a violent separatist movement, the separatist movement was not denounced. In fact, the ETA announcement reinforced the struggle for the Basque homeland, but through the use of democratic means.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-youtube1_98-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-youtube1-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It is crucial to understand that this event may not alter the goals of the Basque separatist movement, but will change the method of the fight for a more autonomous state. Negotiations with the newly elected administration may prove difficult with the return to the center-right People's Party, which is replacing Socialist control, due to pressure from within the party to refuse all ETA negotiations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Victims.2C_tactics_and_attacks">
       Victims, tactics and attacks
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Victims, tactics and attacks">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Their aspiration, which was outlined in 1995 in their
      <i>
       Democratic Alternative
      </i>
      publication, is to force the governments of Spain and France to agree on the following:
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
       <a href="#cite_note-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Recognition of the right to "self-determination and territoriality" for
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euskal_Herria" title="Euskal Herria">
        Euskal Herria
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       That the Basque citizenry are the "unique subject" ("subject" in the sense of "one who acts") to make decisions about the future of the Basque Country.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Amnesty" title="Amnesty">
        Amnesty
       </a>
       for all members, whether prisoners or self-imposed exiles.
      </li>
      <li>
       Respect for "the results of the democratic process in the Basque Country"
      </li>
      <li>
       "Total ceasefire" once these points are guaranteed through a political agreement.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      The group has adopted from time to time other secondary tactical causes such as fighting against:
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Central_nuclear_de_Lem%C3%B3niz_(Vista_Este).JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Central_nuclear_de_Lem%C3%B3niz_%28Vista_Este%29.JPG/220px-Central_nuclear_de_Lem%C3%B3niz_%28Vista_Este%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Central_nuclear_de_Lem%C3%B3niz_%28Vista_Este%29.JPG/330px-Central_nuclear_de_Lem%C3%B3niz_%28Vista_Este%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Central_nuclear_de_Lem%C3%B3niz_%28Vista_Este%29.JPG/440px-Central_nuclear_de_Lem%C3%B3niz_%28Vista_Este%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Central_nuclear_de_Lem%C3%B3niz_(Vista_Este).JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The unfinished
        <a href="/wiki/Lemoniz_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Lemoniz Nuclear Power Plant">
         Lemoniz power plant
        </a>
        in 2006
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Alleged heroin traffickers, as "corrupters of Basque youth" and police collaborators, a
       <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fix" title="wiktionary:fix">
        fix
       </a>
       for a
       <a href="/wiki/Informant" title="Informant">
        tip
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power_plant" title="Nuclear power plant">
        nuclear power plant
       </a>
       facilities at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lemoniz" title="Lemoniz">
        Lemoniz
       </a>
       (Biscay). In the early 1980s, when the Basque ecologist movement opposed
       <a href="/wiki/Lemoniz_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Lemoniz Nuclear Power Plant">
        this project
       </a>
       , ETA joined this point of view and started a series of attacks against the power plant. Five workers were assassinated by the group, including the execution of a kidnapped engineer
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jose_Maria_Ryan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jose Maria Ryan (page does not exist)">
        Jose Maria Ryan
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kapdzy_104-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kapdzy-104">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         104
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The site remains deserted.
      </li>
      <li>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Autov%C3%ADa_A-15" title="Autova A-15">
        A-15
       </a>
       highway which was to run through the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leizaran" title="Leizaran">
        Leizaran
       </a>
       Valley between Navarre and Guipuzcoa. It was inaugurated in 1995, during the construction four people related to the construction were killed by ETA,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kapdzy_104-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-kapdzy-104">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         104
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       and over
       <span class="nowrap">
        280 million
       </span>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pesetas" title="Pesetas">
        pesetas
       </a>
       were spent by public institutions to cover the losses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOPV_105-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BOPV-105">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         105
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BOPN_106-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BOPN-106">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         106
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       The so-called
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_Y" title="Basque Y">
        Basque Y
       </a>
       , a plan to make the
       <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">
        AVE
       </a>
       high-speed railways connect the three capital cities of the Basque Autonomous Community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TAV_107-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-TAV-107">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         107
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In December 2008, the group killed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ignacio_Uria_Mendizabal" title="Ignacio Uria Mendizabal">
        Ignacio Uria Mendizabal
       </a>
       , the Basque owner of one of the companies working in this project.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         108
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In January 2009, ETA threatened that engineers, senior technicians and executives of companies involved in the construction of the high-speed train line would be targets for assassination as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AVE_109-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-AVE-109">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         109
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Victims">
       Victims
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Victims">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      ETA's targets have expanded from the former military/police-related personnel and their families, to a wider array, which today includes the following:
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
         <span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2009)">
          clarification needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Txema_Agirre_Plaza_placa.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2189" data-file-width="3061" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Txema_Agirre_Plaza_placa.jpg/220px-Txema_Agirre_Plaza_placa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Txema_Agirre_Plaza_placa.jpg/330px-Txema_Agirre_Plaza_placa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Txema_Agirre_Plaza_placa.jpg/440px-Txema_Agirre_Plaza_placa.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Txema_Agirre_Plaza_placa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Flowers and a plate remember Ertzaina Txema Agirre, shot dead by ETA gunmen in 1997 while protecting the
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Bilbao_Museum" title="Guggenheim Bilbao Museum">
         Guggenheim Bilbao Museum
        </a>
        (visible on the background)
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Spanish military and police personnel, active duty or retired.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
        <a href="#cite_note-110">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         110
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The barracks of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guardia_Civil_(Spain)" title="Guardia Civil (Spain)">
        Guardia Civil
       </a>
       also provide housing for their families, thus, attacks on the barracks have also resulted in deaths of relatives, including children. As the regional police (
       <a href="/wiki/Ertzaintza" title="Ertzaintza">
        Ertzaintza
       </a>
       in the Basque Country and
       <a href="/wiki/Mossos_d%27Esquadra" title="Mossos d'Esquadra">
        Mossos d'Esquadra
       </a>
       in Catalonia) took a greater role in combating ETA, they were added to their list of targets.
      </li>
      <li>
       Businessmen (such as
       <a href="/wiki/Javier_Ybarra_Berg%C3%A9" title="Javier Ybarra Berg">
        Javier Ybarra
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joxe_Mari_Korta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joxe Mari Korta (page does not exist)">
        Joxe Mari Korta
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ignacio_Uria_Mendizabal" title="Ignacio Uria Mendizabal">
        Ignacio Uria Mendizabal
       </a>
       ):
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         111
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       these are mainly targeted in order to
       <a href="/wiki/Extortion" title="Extortion">
        extort
       </a>
       them for the so-called "
       <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary_tax" title="Revolutionary tax">
        revolutionary tax
       </a>
       ". Refusal to pay has been punished with assassinations, kidnappings for ransom or bombings of their business.
      </li>
      <li>
       Prison officers such as
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Ortega_Lara" title="Jos Antonio Ortega Lara">
        Jos Antonio Ortega Lara
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       Elected parliamentarians, city councillors and ex-councillors, politicians in general: most prominently
       <a href="/wiki/Luis_Carrero_Blanco" title="Luis Carrero Blanco">
        Luis Carrero Blanco
       </a>
       , killed in 1973). Dozens of politicians belonging to the
       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">
        People's Party
       </a>
       (PP) and
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">
        Spanish Socialist Workers' Party
       </a>
       (PSOE) have been assassinated or maimed. Some Basque nationalist politicians from the PNV party, such as
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_Mari_Atutxa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Juan Mari Atutxa (page does not exist)">
        Juan Mari Atutxa
       </a>
       , have also received threats. Hundreds of politicians in Spain require a constant bodyguard service. Bodyguards are contingent victims as well. In 2005 ETA announced that it would no longer "target" elected politicians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
        <a href="#cite_note-112">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         112
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nonetheless, ETA killed ex-council member
       <a href="/wiki/Isa%C3%ADas_Carrasco" title="Isaas Carrasco">
        Isaas Carrasco
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Mondrag%C3%B3n" title="Mondragn">
        Mondragon/Arrasate
       </a>
       on 7 March 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
        <a href="#cite_note-113">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         113
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Balmasedako_auzitegia_2006.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1513" data-file-width="1882" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Balmasedako_auzitegia_2006.jpg/220px-Balmasedako_auzitegia_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Balmasedako_auzitegia_2006.jpg/330px-Balmasedako_auzitegia_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Balmasedako_auzitegia_2006.jpg/440px-Balmasedako_auzitegia_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Balmasedako_auzitegia_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Repairs to the
        <a href="/wiki/Balmaseda" title="Balmaseda">
         Balmaseda
        </a>
        law courts after a bombing in 2006
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Judges and prosecutors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         114
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Particularly threatened are the members of the Spanish anti-terrorist court: the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Audiencia_Nacional_(Spain)" title="Audiencia Nacional (Spain)">
         Audiencia Nacional
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       University professors who publicly express ideas that counter armed Basque separatism: such as
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Broseta" title="Manuel Broseta">
        Manuel Broseta
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Tom%C3%A1s_y_Valiente" title="Francisco Toms y Valiente">
        Francisco Toms y Valiente
       </a>
       . In the latter case, the shooting resulted in more than half a million people protesting against ETA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         115
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Journalists: some of these professionals began to be labeled by ETA as targets starting with the killing of journalist
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Luis_L%C3%B3pez_de_la_Calle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jos Luis Lpez de la Calle (page does not exist)">
        Jos Luis Lpez de la Calle
       </a>
       , assassinated in May 2000.
      </li>
      <li>
       Economic targets: a wide array of private or public property considered valuable assets of Spain, especially railroads, tourist sites, industries, or malls.
      </li>
      <li>
       Exceptionally, ETA has also assassinated former ETA members such as
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Maria_Dolores_Gonz%C3%A1lez_Catarain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Maria Dolores Gonzlez Catarain (page does not exist)">
        Maria Dolores Gonzlez Catarain
       </a>
       as a reprisal for having left the group.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hizrqw_116-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-hizrqw-116">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         116
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       A number of ETA attacks by car bomb have caused random civilian casualties, like ETA's bloodiest attack,
       <a href="/wiki/1987_Hipercor_bombing" title="1987 Hipercor bombing">
        the bombing in 1987
       </a>
       of the subterranean parking lot of the Hipercor supermarket in Barcelona
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
        <a href="#cite_note-117">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         117
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         118
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       which killed 21 civilians and left 45 seriously wounded, of whom 20 were left disabled; also the attack of Plaza de Callao in Madrid.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         119
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Tactics">
       Tactics
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tactics">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      ETA's tactics include:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Direct attacks: killing by shooting the victim in the
       <a href="/wiki/Nape" title="Nape">
        nape
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         120
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         121
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
        <a href="#cite_note-122">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         122
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Bombings (often with
       <a href="/wiki/Car_bomb" title="Car bomb">
        car bombs
       </a>
       ). When the bombs target individuals for assassination they are made by rigging their cars with a bomb. The detonating systems vary: they are rarely manually ignited, but wired so the bomb may explode at ignition or when the car goes over a set speed limit, in the case the bomb is attached directly to the target victim vehicle. Sometimes the bomb is placed inside a stolen car with false plates, parked in the route of the objective, and the explosive remotely activated once the target passes by (i.e., V.I.P. cars, police patrols or military vehicles).
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      These bombs have sometimes killed family members of ETA's target victim and bystanders. When the bombs are large car-bombs seeking to produce large damage and terror, they are generally announced by one or more telephone calls made to newspapers speaking in the name of ETA. Charities (usually
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Detente_Y_Ayuda&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Detente Y Ayuda (page does not exist)">
       Detente Y Ayuda
      </a>
      DYA) have also been used to announce the threat if the bomb is in a populated area. The type of explosives used in these attacks were initially
      <a href="/wiki/Goma-2" title="Goma-2">
       Goma-2
      </a>
      or self-produced
      <a href="/wiki/Ammonal" title="Ammonal">
       ammonal
      </a>
      . After a number of successful robberies in France, ETA began using
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Titadyne" title="Titadyne">
       Titadyne
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Shell_(projectile)" title="Shell (projectile)">
        Shells
       </a>
       : hand-made
       <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">
        mortars
       </a>
       (the
       <i>
        Jo ta ke
       </i>
       model)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         123
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       have been used occasionally to attack military or police bases. Their lack of precision is probably the reason they are not used anymore.
      </li>
      <li>
       Anonymous threats: often delivered in the Basque Country by placards or graffiti. Such threats have forced many people into hiding or into exile from the Basque Country, and have been used to prevent people from freely expressing political ideas other than Basque nationalist ones.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Extortion" title="Extortion">
        Extortion
       </a>
       or blackmail: called by ETA a "revolutionary tax", ETA demands money from a business owner in the Basque Country or elsewhere in Spain, under threats to him and his family, up to and including death threats. Occasionally some French Basques have also been threatened in this manner, such as footballer
       <a href="/wiki/Bixente_Lizarazu" title="Bixente Lizarazu">
        Bixente Lizarazu
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         124
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       ETA moves the extorted funds to accounts in
       <a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">
        Liechtenstein
       </a>
       and other fiscal havens.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         125
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to French judiciary sources, ETA exacts an estimated 900,000 euros a year in this manner.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         126
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       Kidnapping: often as a punishment for failing to pay the blackmail known as "revolutionary tax", but also has been used to try to force the government to free ETA's prisoners under the threat of killing the kidnapped, as in the kidnapping and subsequent execution of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miguel_Angel_Blanco" title="Miguel Angel Blanco">
        Miguel Angel Blanco
       </a>
       . ETA hides the kidnapped in underground chambers without windows, called
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zulos&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zulos (page does not exist)">
         zulos
        </a>
       </i>
       , of very reduced dimensions for extended periods.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         127
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         128
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Also, people robbed of their vehicles are usually tied and abandoned in an isolated place to allow those who assaulted them to escape.
      </li>
      <li>
       Robbery: ETA members rob weapons, explosives, machines for license plates and vehicles.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Attacks">
       Attacks
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Attacks">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_ETA_attacks" title="List of ETA attacks">
       List of ETA attacks
      </a>
     </div>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Activity">
       Activity
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Activity">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      With its attacks against what they consider "enemies of the Basque people", ETA has killed over 820 people since 1968 to date, including more than 340 civilians.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist.com_129-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-economist.com-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It has maimed hundreds more
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-smithsonianmag.com_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-smithsonianmag.com-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and kidnapped dozens.
     </p>
     <p>
      Its ability to inflict violence has declined steadily since the group was at its strongest during the late 1970s and 1980 (when it managed to kill 92 people in a single year).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist.com_129-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-economist.com-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After decreasing peaks in the fatal casualties in 1987 and 1991, 2000 remains to date as the last year when ETA could kill more than 20 in a single year. Since 2002 to date, the yearly number of ETA's fatal casualties has been reduced to single digits.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-economist.com_129-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-economist.com-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Similarly, over the 1990s and, especially, during the 2000s (decade), fluid cooperation between the French and Spanish police, state of the art tracking devices and techniques and, apparently, police
      <a href="/wiki/Mole_(espionage)" title="Mole (espionage)">
       infiltration
      </a>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_84-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      have allowed increasingly repeating blows to ETA's leadership and structure (between May 2008 and April 2009 no less than four consecutive "military chiefs" were arrested
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes.com_84-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-nytimes.com-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ).
     </p>
     <p>
      ETA operates mainly in Spain, particularly in the Basque Country, Navarre, and (to a lesser degree) Madrid, Barcelona, and the tourist areas of the Spanish Mediterranean coast. To date, about 65% of ETA's killings have been committed in the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_Country_(autonomous_community)" title="Basque Country (autonomous community)">
       Basque Country
      </a>
      , followed by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madrid_(autonomous_community)" title="Madrid (autonomous community)">
       Madrid
      </a>
      with roughly 15%.
      <a href="/wiki/Navarre" title="Navarre">
       Navarre
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
       Catalonia
      </a>
      also register significant numbers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Actions in France usually consist of assaults on arsenals or military industries in order to steal weapons or explosives; these are usually stored in large quantities in hide-outs located in the French Basque Country rather than Spain. The French judge
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Laurence_Le_Vert&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Laurence Le Vert (page does not exist)">
       Laurence Le Vert
      </a>
      has been threatened by ETA and a plot arguably aiming to assassinate her was unveiled.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
       <a href="#cite_note-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Only very rarely have ETA members engaged in shootings with the French
      <a href="/wiki/Gendarmerie" title="Gendarmerie">
       Gendarmerie
      </a>
      . This has often occurred mainly when members of the group were confronted at checkpoints.
     </p>
     <p>
      In spite of this, ETA killed in France on 1 December 2007, two Spanish
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guardia_Civil" title="Guardia Civil">
       Civil Guards
      </a>
      on counter-terrorist surveillance duties in
      <a href="/wiki/Capbreton" title="Capbreton">
       Capbreton
      </a>
      , Landes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This has been its first killing after it ended its 2006 declaration of "permanent ceasefire" and the first killing committed by ETA in France of a Spanish police agent ever since 1976, when they kidnapped, tortured and assassinated two Spanish inspectors in
      <a href="/wiki/Hendaye" title="Hendaye">
       Hendaye
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
       <a href="#cite_note-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Financing">
       Financing
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Financing">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      More recently, 2007 police reports point out that, after the serious blows suffered by ETA and its political counterparts during the 2000s (decade), its budget would have been adjusted to 2,000,000 euros annually.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Although ETA used robbery as a means of financing its activities in its early days, it has since been accused both of arms trafficking and of benefiting economically from its political counterpart Batasuna.
      <a href="/wiki/Extortion" title="Extortion">
       Extortion
      </a>
      remains ETA's main source of funds.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Basque_Nationalist_context">
       Basque Nationalist context
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Basque Nationalist context">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      ETA is considered to form part of what is informally known as the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_National_Liberation_Movement" title="Basque National Liberation Movement">
       Basque National Liberation Movement
      </a>
      , a movement born much after ETA's creation. This loose term refers to a range of political organizations that are ideologically akin, comprising several distinct organizations that promote a type of
      <a href="/wiki/Left-wing_politics" title="Left-wing politics">
       leftist
      </a>
      Basque nationalism that is often referred to by the Basque-language term
      <i>
       Ezker
       <a href="/wiki/Abertzale" title="Abertzale">
        Abertzalea
       </a>
      </i>
      (Nationalist Left). Other groups typically considered to belong to this independentist movement are: the political party
      <a href="/wiki/Batasuna" title="Batasuna">
       Batasuna
      </a>
      , the nationalist youth organization
      <a href="/wiki/Segi_(organization)" title="Segi (organization)">
       Segi
      </a>
      , the labour union
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Langile_Abertzaleen_Batzordeak" title="Langile Abertzaleen Batzordeak">
       Langile Abertzaleen Batzordeak
      </a>
      (LAB), and
      <a href="/wiki/Askatasuna" title="Askatasuna">
       Askatasuna
      </a>
      among others. There are often strong interconnections between these groups, double or even triple membership are not infrequent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jvjtfe_35-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-jvjtfe-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      There are Basque nationalist parties with similar goals as those of ETA (namely, independence) but who openly reject their violent means. They are:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EAJ-PNV" title="EAJ-PNV">
       EAJ-PNV
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Eusko_Alkartasuna" title="Eusko Alkartasuna">
       Eusko Alkartasuna
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Aralar_Party" title="Aralar Party">
       Aralar
      </a>
      and, in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Basque_country" title="French Basque country">
       French Basque country
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Abertzaleen_Batasuna" title="Abertzaleen Batasuna">
       Abertzaleen Batasuna
      </a>
      . In addition, a number of left-wing parties, such as
      <a href="/wiki/United_Left_(Spain)" title="United Left (Spain)">
       Ezker Batua
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Batzarre" title="Batzarre">
       Batzarre
      </a>
      and some sectors of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EAJ-PNV" title="EAJ-PNV">
       EAJ-PNV
      </a>
      party, also support self-determination but are not in favour of independence.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="French_role">
       French role
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: French role">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Historically, members of ETA have taken refuge in France, particularly the
      <a href="/wiki/French_Basque_Country" title="French Basque Country">
       French Basque Country
      </a>
      . The leadership have typically chosen to live in France for security reasons, where police pressure is much less than in Spain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_135-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-telegraph-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Accordingly, ETA's tactical approach had been to downplay the issue of independence of the French Basque country so as to get French acquiescence for their activities. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_government" title="French government">
       French government
      </a>
      quietly tolerated the group, especially during
      <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">
       Franco's regime
      </a>
      , when ETA members could face the death penalty in Spain. In the 1980s, the advent of the
      <a href="/wiki/Grupos_Antiterroristas_de_Liberaci%C3%B3n" title="Grupos Antiterroristas de Liberacin">
       GAL
      </a>
      still hindered
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Counter-terrorist" title="Counter-terrorist">
       counter-terrorist
      </a>
      cooperation between the France and Spain, with the French government considering ETA a Spanish domestic problem. At the time, ETA members often travelled to and from between the two countries using the French sanctuary as a base for operations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      With the disbanding of the GAL, the French government considered that detainees' rights were being adequately defended in Spain. France changed its position in the matter and initiated in the 1990s the ongoing period of active cooperation with the Spanish government against ETA, including fast-track transfers of detainees to Spanish tribunals that are regarded as fully compliant with
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      legislation in human rights and the legal representation of detainees. Virtually all of the highest ranks within ETA including their successive "military", "political" or finances chiefs have been captured in French territory, from where they had been plotting their activities after having crossed the border from Spain.
     </p>
     <p>
      In response to the new situation, ETA carried out attacks against French policemen and made threats to some French judges and prosecutors. This implied a change from the group's previous low-profile in the French Basque Country, which successive ETA leaders had used to discreetly manage their activities in Spain.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_135-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-telegraph-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_response">
       Government response
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Government response">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      ETA considers its prisoners
      <a href="/wiki/Political_prisoner" title="Political prisoner">
       political prisoners
      </a>
      . Until 2003,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      ETA consequently forbade them to ask penal authorities for progression to
      <i>
       tercer grado
      </i>
      (a form of
      <a href="/wiki/Open_prison" title="Open prison">
       open prison
      </a>
      that allows single-day or weekend
      <a href="/wiki/Furlough" title="Furlough">
       furloughs
      </a>
      ) or parole. Before that date, those who did so were menaced and expelled from the group. Some were assassinated by ETA for leaving the group and going through reinsertion programs.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hizrqw_116-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-hizrqw-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Spanish Government passed the
      <i>
       Ley de Partidos Polticos
      </i>
      . This is a law barring political parties which support violence and do not condemn terrorist actions or are involved with terrorist groups.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ley_6.2F2002_138-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Ley_6.2F2002-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The law resulted in the banning of
      <a href="/wiki/Herri_Batasuna" title="Herri Batasuna">
       Herri Batasuna
      </a>
      and its successor parties unless they explicitly condemned terrorist actions and, at times, imprisoning or trying some of its leaders who have been indicted for cooperation with ETA.
     </p>
     <p>
      Judge
      <a href="/wiki/Baltasar_Garz%C3%B3n" title="Baltasar Garzn">
       Baltasar Garzn
      </a>
      has initiated a judicial procedure (coded as
      <i>
       18/98
      </i>
      ), aimed towards the support structure of ETA. This procedure started in 1998 with the preventive closure of the newspaper
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Egin_(newspaper)" title="Egin (newspaper)">
        Egin
       </a>
      </i>
      (and its associated radio-station
      <i>
       Egin Irratia
      </i>
      ), accused of being linked to ETA, and temporary imprisoning the editor of its "investigative unit",
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pepe_Rei&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pepe Rei (page does not exist)">
       Pepe Rei
      </a>
      , under similar accusations. In August 1999 Judge
      <a href="/wiki/Baltasar_Garz%C3%B3n" title="Baltasar Garzn">
       Baltasar Garzn
      </a>
      authorized the reopening of the newspaper and the radio, but they could not reopen due to economic difficulties.
     </p>
     <p>
      Judicial procedure 18/98 has many ramifications, including the following:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       A trial against a little-known organization called
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Xaki&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Xaki (page does not exist)">
         Xaki
        </a>
       </i>
       , acquitted in 2001 as the "international network" of ETA.
      </li>
      <li>
       A trial against the youths' movement
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jarrai&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jarrai (page does not exist)">
         Jarrai
        </a>
       </i>
       -
       <i>
        Haika
       </i>
       -
       <i>
        Segi
       </i>
       , accused of contributing to street violence in an organized form and in connivance with ETA.
      </li>
      <li>
       Another trial against
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Pepe_Rei&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Pepe Rei (page does not exist)">
        Pepe Rei
       </a>
       and his new investigation magazine
       <i>
        Ardi Beltza
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Black Sheep
       </i>
       ). The magazine was also closed down.
      </li>
      <li>
       A trial against the political organization
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ekin" title="Ekin">
         Ekin
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        Action
       </i>
       ), accused of promoting
       <a href="/wiki/Civil_disobedience" title="Civil disobedience">
        civil disobedience
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       A trial against the organization
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Joxemi_Zumalabe_Fundazioa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Joxemi Zumalabe Fundazioa (page does not exist)">
         Joxemi Zumalabe Fundazioa
        </a>
       </i>
       , which was once again accused of promoting civil disobedience.
      </li>
      <li>
       A trial against the prisoner support movement
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Amnistiaren_Aldeko_Komiteak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Amnistiaren Aldeko Komiteak (page does not exist)">
         Amnistiaren Aldeko Komiteak
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       A trial against
       <a href="/wiki/Batasuna" title="Batasuna">
        Batasuna
       </a>
       and the
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Herriko_Tabernak&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Herriko Tabernak (page does not exist)">
         Herriko Tabernak
        </a>
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        people's taverns
       </i>
       ), accused of acting as a network of meeting centres for members and supporters of ETA. Batasuna was outlawed in all forms. Most taverns continue working normally as their ownership is not directly linked to Batasuna.
      </li>
      <li>
       A trial against the league of Basque-language academies
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alfabetatze_Euskalduntze_Koordinakundea&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alfabetatze Euskalduntze Koordinakundea (page does not exist)">
        AEK
       </a>
       . The case was dropped in 2001.
      </li>
      <li>
       Another trial against
       <i>
        Ekin
       </i>
       , accusing
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Iker_Casnova&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Iker Casnova (page does not exist)">
        Iker Casnova
       </a>
       of managing the finances of ETA.
      </li>
      <li>
       A trial against the association of Basque municipalities
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Udalbiltza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Udalbiltza (page does not exist)">
        Udalbiltza
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       The closing of the newspaper
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euskaldunon_Egunkaria" title="Euskaldunon Egunkaria">
        Euskaldunon Egunkaria
       </a>
       in 2003 and the imprisonment and trial of its editor,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Martxelo_Otamendi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Martxelo Otamendi (page does not exist)">
        Martxelo Otamendi
       </a>
       , due to links with ETA accounting and fundraising, and other journalists (some of whom reported torture).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Otamendi_139-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Otamendi-139">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         139
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <p>
      As of June 2007
      <sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
       <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit">
        [update]
       </a>
      </sup>
      , indicted members of the youth movements Haika, Segi and Jarrai have been found guilty (January 2007) of a crime of
      <a href="/wiki/Connivance" title="Connivance">
       connivance
      </a>
      with terrorism. Most of the other trials are still under process.
     </p>
     <p>
      On Tuesday 20 May 2008, leading ETA figures were arrested in
      <a href="/wiki/Bordeaux" title="Bordeaux">
       Bordeaux
      </a>
      , France.
      <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Javier_L%C3%B3pez_Pe%C3%B1a" title="Francisco Javier Lpez Pea">
       Francisco Javier Lpez Pea
      </a>
      , also known as 'Thierry,' had been on the run for twenty years before his arrest.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A final total of arrests brought in six people, including ETA members and supporters, including the ex-Mayor of
      <a href="/wiki/Andoain" title="Andoain">
       Andoain
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jos%C3%A9_Antonio_Barandiar%C3%A1n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jos Antonio Barandiarn (page does not exist)">
       Jos Antonio Barandiarn
      </a>
      , who is rumoured to have led police to 'Thierry'.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
       <a href="#cite_note-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Spanish Interior Ministry claimed the relevance of the arrests would come in time with the investigation. Furthermore, the Interior Minister said that those members of ETA now arrested had ordered the latest attacks, and that senior ETA member Francisco Javier Lpez Pea was "not just another arrest because he is, in all probability, the man who has most political and military weight in the terrorist group."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After Lopez Pena's arrest, along with the
      <a href="/wiki/Basque_referendum,_2008" title="Basque referendum, 2008">
       Basque referendum
      </a>
      being put on hold, police work has been on the rise. On 22 July 2008, Spanish police dismantled the most active cell of ETA by detaining nine suspected members of the group.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interior_Minister" title="Interior Minister">
       Interior Minister
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfredo_Perez_Rubalcaba" title="Alfredo Perez Rubalcaba">
       Alfredo Perez Rubalcaba
      </a>
      said about the arrests: "We can't say this is the only ETA unit but it was the most active, most dynamic and of course the most wanted one."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Four days later French police also arrested two suspects believed to be tied to the same active cell. The two suspects were: Asier Eceiza, considered a top aide to a senior ETA operative still sought by police, and Olga Comes, whom authorities have linked to the ETA suspects.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144">
       <a href="#cite_note-144">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        144
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="International_response">
       International response
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: International response">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
       European Union
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._State_Department_list_of_Foreign_Terrorist_Organizations" title="U.S. State Department list of Foreign Terrorist Organizations">
       United States
      </a>
      list ETA as a
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_designated_terrorist_groups" title="List of designated terrorist groups">
       terrorist group
      </a>
      in their relevant watch lists. The United Kingdom lists ETA as a terrorist group under the
      <a href="/wiki/Terrorism_Act_2000" title="Terrorism Act 2000">
       Terrorism Act 2000
      </a>
      . The
      <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
       Canadian Parliament
      </a>
      listed ETA as a terrorist group in 2003.
     </p>
     <p>
      France and Spain have often shown co-operation in the fight against ETA, after France's lack of co-operation during the Franco era. In late 2007, two Spanish guards were shot to death in France when on a joint operation with their French counterparts. Furthermore, in May 2008, the arrests of four people in Bordeaux led to a major breakthrough against ETA, according to the Spanish Interior Ministry.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145">
       <a href="#cite_note-145">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        145
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On 2 October 2008, as ETA activity increased, France increased its pressure on ETA by arresting more ETA suspects, including
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Unai_Fano&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Unai Fano (page does not exist)">
       Unai Fano
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mar%C3%ADa_Lizarraga&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mara Lizarraga (page does not exist)">
       Mara Lizarraga
      </a>
      on 23 September.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
       <a href="#cite_note-146">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        146
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Esteban_Murillo_Zubiri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Esteban Murillo Zubiri (page does not exist)">
       Esteban Murillo Zubiri
      </a>
      , brother of
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gabriel_Zuburi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gabriel Zuburi (page does not exist)">
       Gabriel Zuburi
      </a>
      ),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147">
       <a href="#cite_note-147">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        147
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bidarrain&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bidarrain (page does not exist)">
       Bidarrain
      </a>
      . He had been wanted by the Spanish authorities since 2007 when a
      <a href="/wiki/Europol" title="Europol">
       Europol
      </a>
      arrest warrant was issued against him. French judicial authorities had already ordered that he be held in prison on remand.
     </p>
     <p>
      Spain has also sought cooperation from the United Kingdom in dealing with ETA-IRA ties. In November 2008, this came to light after
      <a href="/wiki/I%C3%B1aki_de_Juana_Chaos" title="Iaki de Juana Chaos">
       Iaki de Juana Chaos
      </a>
      , whose release from prison was canceled on appeal, had moved to
      <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">
       Belfast
      </a>
      . He was thought to be staying at an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Provisional_IRA" title="Provisional IRA">
       IRA
      </a>
      safe house while being sought by the Spanish authorities. Interpol notified the judge, Eloy Velasco, that he was in either the Republic of Ireland or
      <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland" title="Northern Ireland">
       Northern Ireland
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148">
       <a href="#cite_note-148">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        148
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_related_armed_groups">
       Other related armed groups
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Other related armed groups">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Disbanded_violent_groups">
       Disbanded violent groups
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Disbanded violent groups">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       Anti-ETA groups:
       <ul>
        <li>
         <i>
          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Acci%C3%B3n_Nacional_Espa%C3%B1ola&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Accin Nacional Espaola (page does not exist)">
           Accin Nacional Espaola
          </a>
         </i>
        </li>
        <li>
         <i>
          ATE (
          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Anti-Terrorismo_ETA&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Anti-Terrorismo ETA (page does not exist)">
           Anti-Terrorismo ETA
          </a>
          )
         </i>
        </li>
        <li>
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Batall%C3%B3n_Vasco_Espa%C3%B1ol" title="Batalln Vasco Espaol">
